## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: The task models the time evolution of a chemical species concentration, which is the fundamental problem in chemical kinetics. The rate dA_dt typically depends on the concentration A through power-law rate laws, and may exhibit time-modulated behavior due to catalyst effects, consecutive pathways, or autocatalysis.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 (constant reaction rate independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay or radioactive decay)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular elementary reaction)
- General nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical or complex reaction orders)
- Autocatalytic kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (reaction accelerated by its own product)
- Time-modulated rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (catalyst deactivation or activation over time)
- Consecutive reaction intermediate: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) - c2 * A (formation from precursor minus decay)
- Induction period kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A * (1 - exp(c1 * t)) (delayed reaction onset due to initiator buildup)
- Diffusion-limited surface reaction: dA_dt = -c0 * A**0.5 (concentration-limited diffusion in porous media)
- Bistable chemical switch: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 * (c1 - A) (cubic nonlinearity enabling multiple steady states)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Integer reaction orders → Pure power-law dependence on concentration (dA_dt ∝ A^n, n=0,1,2)
- Autocatalytic behavior → Polynomial terms mixing A and (c - A) producing sigmoidal rate profiles
- Consecutive reaction intermediates → Superposition of formation and decay terms (sum of exponentials or linear combination of exp and A)
- Diffusion-controlled limits → Fractional power-law dependence on concentration (e.g., A**0.5) or square-root time scaling
- Catalyst deactivation/activation → Multiplicative time-modulating factors (e.g., A * exp(c*t)) altering the effective rate constant
- Induction/lag phases → Delay factors subtracted from unity or difference of exponentials multiplying the base rate law
- Bistable/oscillatory switches → Cubic or higher-order nonlinear concentration terms enabling multiple steady states or limit cycles
- Stoichiometric pathway coupling → Linear combinations of polynomial concentration terms reflecting parallel or sequential reaction steps

### Analysis of Candidates

The Ground Truth (GT) function simplifies to a quadratic polynomial in `A` plus a sine-of-logarithm term:
`GT(A) = k1*A**2 + k2*A + k3*sin(log(A + 1))`
where `k1 = -0.678959`, `k2 = -0.678959`, `k3 = 0.164069`. The variable `t` only appears as a fixed constant multiplier in the GT and does not affect the functional form with respect to `A`. GT Equivalence Verification (CRK8)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A**c1 - c2*A + c3*_t*sin(log(A + c4))
Candidates evaluated: 59
Matched candidate IDs: [6, 39, 40, 41, 42, 43, 44]
Matched candidates: ["A*c0*(A + c1) + c2 + c3*sin(c4*log(A*c5 + 1) + c6)", "A*(A*c0 + c1) + c2*sin(log(A + 1))", "A*c0 + c1*Abs(A)**2 + c2*sin(log(Abs(A) + 1))", "A**2*c0 + A*c1 + c2*sin(log(Abs(A) + 1))", "A**2*c0 + A*c1 + c2*sin(log(A + 1))", "A*c0*(A + 1) + c1*sin(log(Abs(A) + 1))", "A*c0*(A + 1) + c1*sin(log(A + 1))"]

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT numerical expression:** `-0.6789593965981179*A**2 - 0.6789593965981179*A + 0.1640697849676163*sin(log(A + 1))`

This is: `c0*A^2 + c1*A + c2*sin(log(A + 1))` where c0 ≈ -0.679, c1 ≈ -0.679, c2 ≈ 0.164.

The GT has three basis components:
1. A quadratic term in A (A² and A terms)
2. sin(log(A + 1))

No exponential terms, no A⁵ terms, no t-dependence (since _t is absorbed into c3).

Let me check each candidate:

**Candidate 1:** Has t-dependence that can't be eliminated (t appears in numerator and denominator differently). Setting c2=0 would simplify but then we'd need to check. If c2=0: `(c0*t + c1 + c3*(A^5*c4 + A*c5*(A+c6) + c7*sin(A*c8+c9)))/c3`. This gives a constant times t plus polynomial + sin terms. The t-dependence remains. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 2:** `A^5*c0 + A*c1*(A+c2) + c3*sin(A*c4+c5) + c6*sin(c7*log(c8*t+1)+c9)`. Has t-dependence and sin(A*c4+c5) instead of sin(log(A+1)). sin(A) ≠ sin(log(A+1)). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 3:** Expanding: `(A*c0+c1)/(A*c2+c3) + A^5*c4 + A*c5*(A+c6) + c7*sin(A*c8+c9)`. Has sin(A*c8+c9) not sin(log(A+1)), and A^5 term. Setting c4=0, still has sin(linear in A) ≠ sin(log(A+1)). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 4:** Has sin(A*c4+c5) and cos(c7*exp(A*c8)). Neither is sin(log(A+1)). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 5:** Expanding: `(A*c0+c1)/(A*c2+c3) + A*c4*(A+c5) + c6 + c7*exp(A*c8)`. No sin(log(A+1)). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 6:** `A*c0*(A+c1) + c2 + c3*sin(c4*log(A*c5+1)+c6)`. This gives `c0*A² + c0*c1*A + c2 + c3*sin(c4*log(c5*A+1)+c6)`. Setting c4=1, c5=1, c6=0: `c0*A² + c0*c1*A + c2 + c3*sin(log(A+1))`. Setting c2=0, c0=-0.679, c1=1, c3=0.164. This gives `-0.679*A² - 0.679*A + 0.164*sin(log(A+1))`. **MATCH!**

Candidate 6 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 7:** Has sin(A*c3+c4) and exp(c6*sin(A*c7+c8)). Neither is sin(log(A+1)). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 39:** `A*(A*c0+c1) + c2*sin(log(A+1))` = `c0*A² + c1*A + c2*sin(log(A+1))`. **MATCH!**
